## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics: nonlinear/forced/damped oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is the acceleration and the features x (position), v (velocity), and t (time) match Newtonian second-order oscillator models where acceleration is determined by restoring forces (often nonlinear in x), damping (often nonlinear in v), and possible external/parametric time-dependent forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = -c0 * x (Hookean restoring force per unit mass)
- Viscously damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (sinusoidal external forcing)
- Driven damped oscillator (general phase): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (phase-shifted periodic forcing)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x^3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring + damping)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x^3 - c2 * x^5 - c3 * v (higher-order elastic nonlinearity)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic drag): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (velocity-squared dissipation, e.g., aerodynamic drag)
- Nonlinear damping (cubic): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v^3 (odd damping nonlinearity near high speeds)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x^2) * v (self-excited oscillations with amplitude regulation)
- Pendulum (exact restoring force): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (angular oscillation with nonlinear sine restoring force)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / parametric pumping)
- LiÃ©nard-type oscillator (general polynomial form): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x^3 - (c2 + c3 * x^2) * v (position-dependent damping with nonlinear stiffness)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd restoring-force symmetry: if the oscillator is symmetric about x=0, dv_dt typically contains odd powers of x (x, x^3, x^5) but not even powers.
- Energy-conserving core vs dissipation: a conservative model has dv_dt depending mainly on x; adding any term proportional to v (or v*Abs(v), v^3) indicates damping and energy loss.
- Self-excitation/limit cycle signature: terms like (c0 - x^2) * v imply negative damping at small |x| and positive damping at large |x|, producing stable oscillation amplitude.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: a +x^3 contribution inside the restoring force changes frequency with amplitude; its sign determines whether frequency increases (hardening) or decreases (softening).
- External periodic forcing: explicit sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms in dv_dt suggest driven response, resonance, and possibly frequency locking.
- Parametric pumping: time-modulated stiffness multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) indicates parametric resonance regions rather than direct forcing.
- Nonlinear drag regimes: v*Abs(v) is characteristic of quadratic drag; v^3 often approximates higher-speed dissipative effects while preserving odd symmetry in v.
- Pendulum-like behavior: sin(c*x) restoring force implies small-angle linearization dv_dt â‰ˆ -c*x but strong nonlinearity near larger amplitudes (period increases with amplitude).

$$GT = -0.493165631499977 \cdot v \cdot (1 - x^2) - 1.16769962902767 \cdot x \cdot \exp(-|x|)$$

Expanding:
$$GT = -0.493165631499977 \cdot v + 0.493165631499977 \cdot v \cdot x^2 - 1.16769962902767 \cdot x \cdot \exp(-|x|)$$

The key components are:
1. A term proportional to $v$
2. A term proportional to $v \cdot x^2$
3. A term $x \cdot \exp(-|x|)$

The critical question is whether $x \cdot \exp(-|x|)$ can be represented by the basis functions in each candidate. Note that $x \cdot \exp(-|x|)$ is NOT a polynomial, NOT a logarithm, NOT a sine, and NOT a simple power law $x^c$ (since $x^c$ doesn't have the exponential decay).

Let me analyze the candidate structures. Most candidates contain terms like:
- $x^{c_i}$ (power law terms)
- $x^3$ (cubic terms)
- $v$, $v \cdot x^2$ (velocity terms)
- Some have $\log$, $\sin$, $v^{c}$, $t$ terms

**Key insight:** $x \cdot \exp(-|x|)$ cannot be exactly represented by:
- Any finite sum of power laws $x^{c_i}$ (these are algebraic, not transcendental with exponential decay)
- Polynomials in $x$
- $\log(cx + 1)$ terms
- $\sin(cx + d)$ terms
- $v^c$ terms
- $t$-dependent terms (GT has no $t$ dependence)

The function $x \cdot e^{-|x|}$ is a specific transcendental function that none of these basis functions can reproduce. Power laws $x^c$ behave as monomials and cannot capture exponential decay. Logarithmic terms $\log(cx+1)$ grow logarithmically. Sine terms oscillate. None of these can exactly equal $x \cdot e^{-|x|}$ for all $x$.

Let me verify: Could a sum of multiple power laws $\sum a_i x^{c_i}$ equal $x \cdot e^{-|x|}$? No - power laws and exponentials are fundamentally different function classes. A finite sum of power laws cannot equal an exponential function over a continuous domain.

Since **every single candidate** uses only combinations of:
- Power laws ($x^c$)
- Polynomials ($x$, $x^3$)
- $v$, $v \cdot x^2$
- Occasionally $\log$, $\sin$, $v^c$, $t$-dependent terms

None can exactly reproduce $x \cdot \exp(-|x|)$.

For candidates with $t$-dependent terms (41, 42, 44, 46, 47, 49, 50): setting $t$ coefficients to 0 removes those terms, leaving the same insufficient basis.

For candidates with $\log$ terms (8, 25-28, 32, 43, 45-47): $\log$ cannot produce exponential decay.

For candidates with $\sin$ terms (29, 45, 48): $\sin$ oscillates and cannot match exponential decay.

For candidates with $v^c$ terms (5-7, 30, 31): these introduce nonlinear $v$ dependence not in GT.

**Every candidate fails** because none contain $\exp(-|x|)$ or any equivalent basis function.
